Steve Fenn<//user_name>
< review>
This is a very good place to have some peace and quiet while enjoying the trails. But, today we were walking up what the Reserve map says is Horned Lizard Bypass  (but Google Maps says it is Rios Canyon Rd). Not too far up that dirt road from the Main Entrance at Horsemill Rd there is a house on a little hill. A German Shepard dog was loose, not on a leash, on that dirt road (Horned Lizard Bypass/Rios Canyon Rd), near the house and attacked our dog, which was on a leash.
Someone should be held accountable.</review>

< Review>
Right now this is a wonderland of blossoms due to the rainy winter. Close enough, but far enough to still be open!</Review>
<date>1589686900016</date></record>
</dataset><record>
<response>None< /response>< review>
This is definitely one of my favorite places to explore nature. In addition to its natural beauty, it holds history, art, and environmental education opportunities. Typically less peopled than places like Mission Trails, this quiet little preserve is a great place for quiet reflection. It's trails vary from stroller friendly to hiker challenging (but I haven't come across anything crazy intense). There is some poison oak in sections of the park, but if you stay on the trails you can easily avoid it. The workers there are working hard to restore certain sections to their original native plants, so be sure to stay on the trails in any case. If you visit, be sure not to miss the mushroomed shaped hay bale house. On a hot day, it is a heavenly cool place to catch your breath, and the mosaic patio and sculptures outside it are truly charming.</review>

<Rate>5</Rate><review>Hidden gem of East County! If you are looking for a great place to hike you have to visit this place. There are a lot of trails. Some are not marked very well, but I am told they are in the process of working on that now. There is a beautiful Oak grove with a huge amount of Engelmann and Coast live oaks that provide a shady spot to walk and explore. There are lots of horseback riders and mountain bikers so don't be surprised if you need to share the trails. You can even bring your dog for a walk, but be sure to keep them on a leash at all times.</review><Pics>None<//Pics><response>None</response><gmap_id>0x80d95f1d3777e4f9:0xc30dca6d1f0fa9fc< /gmap_id></record>

< Text>
This review is going to be a long one, but I am going to make it as honest and unbiased as possible and want it to be clear that this is MY experience with Desert Auto Dealer (obviously experiences vary).

I bought a 2006 BMW 325i (manual transmission) about 2 weeks ago.  The car from the outside was gorgeous, just a few minor details but then again it is a used vehicle.  The initial visit went great, the guys are very friendly; great salesmen.  I left a $200 "deposit" since I had to wait for the check to arrive, mind you, I live in 29 Palms, CA.  Before I get to what's coming next, let me say I blame myself for not inspecting the vehicle the way I know that It's supposed to be inspected (I've been working on cars since I was 11), and not them.

Let's fast forward to the day I actually picked up the car.  While driving at highway speeds, I started to notice a very loose steering wheel and the "humming" noise that's typical with a wheel bearing going bad.  At this point I wasnt alarmed because again "used vehicle", this was more of a routune maintenance issue; however, it got me curious.

When I got home to inspect the car, here's what I came across: hood lifts did not work, tie rods were bad (both inner and outer),  valve cover gasket leaks oil, power steering reservoir leaks fluid, hoses to PS pump leak, both front wheel bearings were bad and most worrisome,  the oil pan gasket is leaking oil tremendously.  I've spent the last 4 days working non-stop to correct some of these issues, not to mention the money that it has cost me! At this point I've invested $800 (and about to increase) in just PARTS; luckily I know how to do all the work myself, but any other person would be stuck with a huge bill.

Lastly, as I stated, I blame myself for not inspecting the car;  because let's face it, the job of these guys is to make money, and I accept that.  What really has me upset is the fact that I still havent even received my "deposit" back, which was stated to be returned to me once I bought the car.  I've called and even sent texts (yes I have screenshots) and after 2 weeks that money is yet to post;  I will be utilizing it to buy more parts for the lemon of a car that I bought.

UPDATE: 2018 SEP 05 -  Received update with regards to funds;  money is currently in pedning status.  Much appreciated.< /Text>

<review>Share review

Embed review

Write an update

9/30/2020
We've been taking our cavalier, Louis, to DogPile since February 2020 and he absolutely loves it! He generally has anxiety and is a stage 5 clinger, but when he realizes we are close to DogPile he starts tugging at his leash and is super excited to go inside. He doesn't even say goodbye to his mom!

DogPile has a huge outdoor/indoor space with lots of room for the pups to run around, Louis is exhausted when he comes home. We like that he's not stuck in a kennel or a small room the entire day. We were able to go inside before the pandemic and it was always clean, didn't smell, and the dogs looked happy and well-cared for. It's super easy to drop off Louis either for the day or if we have errands to run. Someone is always there and they are flexible with drop-off/pick-ups. The prices are reasonable and the DogPile team could not be nicer! They post pictures and videos on instagram (@dogpiledogs) and it's fun to see Louis and the other pups playing.< /review><date>1601497569838< /date></record></dataset><record>

<Rating>5<//Rating>< review>
I have been bringing our dog here for about 6 months. She and I love it here. The staff is super friendly and responsive. There is off-street parking for easy drop-off and pick up. The facility is clean and spacious with a great drop-off entry area. The facility is separated by big and small dogs, and both have in-door and out-door play areas. The dogs are always calm at any time of day, and I have never heard a dog bark once while I am there! When I pick up my dog at the end of the day, classical music is playing, I can see my dog lounging on a dog cot, and she is exhausted from playing all day. We just left here for a week over the holidays, and when we picked her up she was definitely tired from a week of playing, but she was calm, and while I know she was probably happy to see me, she we was just super chilled-out. I cannot recommend Dogpile Dogs enough.< /review>

<Rate>4< /Rate><Review>I dined there two nights in a row, as my hotel was just across the street. The dining room is nice, not too loud, considering the amount of tables set up. Their wine selection was good, but a tad expensive for selections by the glass. I thought their spinach ravioli was the better of the two meals I had. The sauce on the ravioli was good enough to dip the bread in, after I polished off all the ravioli. The bread was warm and tasty, and came with oil and vinegar. The second night, I had their free range chicken, with a (slightly) spicy sauce. The chicken was cooked very well, and the spinach side was prepared perfectly. The potatoes that came with the dish were the only low point, as they were somewhat hard and dry. Service was attentive, but just a tiny bit on the slow side one evening. Still, the waiter was friendly. I watched him go over almost the entire menu with a table of four next to me, after they just couldn't decide what to order. <Response>None<//Response><Text>My girlfriend and I went there for our 1 year anniversary because we wanted to splurge a little. Side note: And also because we're boycotting Olive Garden for supporting Trump's reelection.

First, the service was great. All of the servers were aware of our needs and were filling up our waters almost every time they walked by. Second, the dinner was absolutely DELICIOUS and SIMPLE.

My girlfriend got the gnocchi al pesto and the pesto, you can tell, is homemade and absolutely delicious with blasts of flavor. I received the penne with the vodka sauce without bacon because we're vegetarian and OH MY WORD, that pasta dish was made with so much jam packed flavor. The sauce was absolutely amazing. You can truly tell this restaurant cares about being authentic and utilizing fresh ingredients that have incredible flavor. It's a quite fancy restaurant with good decor and ambience. The people who work there seemed to behave as if they know of such a situation. We went twice thIs particular week as it was close and for the guests. However, the experience during the two visits last week was less than satisfactory.

Perhaps, it was too busy. But, it was difficult to get attention. Upon getting the attention and asking for a few things, it took several minutes to respond making what were requested more or less meaningless for the meal.

One of the guest's meal was subpar where the parts of the spaghetti pasta were clumped and thus undercooked, causing some efforts to avoid those portions. In fact, my fish/salmon was undercooked in retrospect, which I thought at the time was intentional. Anyway, the guest was gracious enough to not cause issues with the pasta and thus found out only toward the end of the meal. We considered bringing this to the attendant but decided not to due to the earlier slow and somewhat ignorant responses and we didn't want to be late to the next event.

Lastly, about the food... It is okay but really it's missing something as the food tends to be blend and doesn't really bring out the exclamatory wows. I should have voiced objection when this was picked bringing up how I got sick (once each at the San Jose and Santa Clara restaurant) after eating at Il Fornaio previously. I am glad that I didn't get sick after eating the undercooked salmon.

Italian cuisine is one of my favorite. But, it's been less than average experience here at Il Fornaio unfortunately, especially when one considers the price...

I considered 1 star rating... The second star is for the decor and ambience...</text>

< text>
Came here for my parents' 30th anniversary lunch. We decided to come to the lower-reviewed San Jose location because it is closer to us and to avoid the lunch rush in Santa Clara.

I have to say that the reviews are right; service was pretty underwhelming. Our server was pretty aloof, and I never caught his name. He seemed a little annoyed about our questions about the menu. He never checked in with us after the food arrived, and we spent about half of our eating time trying to locate him to get our glasses refilled and order a drink. We felt like we were interrupting him. What for the food was also pretty long, but that doesn't usually bother us. Has some nice date night ambience, but it was kind of spoiled by the service.

The food was solid. We have had Il Fornaio catering that has blown us away, and this didn't do that. With the exception of the bruschetta, which was excellent. Petto di Pollo a la Peperonccini - essentially a grilled chicken with a spicy sauce and a kind of boring salad. Ravioli - Good! The sauce was very fresh tasting with a bit of bit. Lasag√±a - good, but very rich. Very soft and sauce-like.

So... probably worth it to go to Santa Clara for the better service. Also, parking validation for Convention Center parking only, just fyi.</text>

<Review>The Olive bread was very good.  After that everything went downhill.  The Caesar salad was not fresh and had some brown pieces in it. It was salty and hands down the worst pizza I have ever had.  The average Italian would think we are idiots for eating such low quality dishes at a sky high price.

<Review>Excellent Italian food served by slightly harried waiters in a comfortable setting. We both chose appetizers and an entree.

My wife had a seafood sampler from the regular menu - it was exceptional with squid, tuna, scallops, and shrimp. There was a light sauce that enhanced, not overpowered, the seafood. I chose the Jota alla Triestina (borlotti bean soup) from their Friuli menu and it was an exceptional rustic soup, hearty but not rich.

We both ordered entrees from the Friuli menu. The Risotto Miramare was excellent with perfect risotto and seafood (shrimp, calamari, crab) in every bite. Balanced with peas and tomatoes it was a fantastic meal. The Gamberoni alla Busara was amazing - prawns larger than some lobster tails sauteed in paprika, garlic, brandy, capers, marinara and cream.

After our food we didn't have dessert because we were full. But I'm excited to check back for their regional specialties coming up.</Review><Rate>5< /Rate>< Date>

<userid>114104347577079556242< /userid><name>Lori Fox<//name><time>1536210634391<//time>< Text>
We stopped in here before a show downtown. The ambiance was ok, it was around 6pm and the afternoon sun was blazing thru the windows making it pretty warm in there. I had the Tagletell bolognese and my husband had the veal. Both were good sized portions. My pasta was great. It was toothsome and perfectly al dente. The bolognese sauce was quite tasty. My husband's veal however, not so good. The sauce was lemony and bright but the veal was tough and the thin coating of flour that should have been crispy was kinda gummy. The vegetable side was a giant broccoli stem and carrot that were undercooked. The food came out fast, which was nice since we were eating pre- show, but we had to ask several times for bread (it finally came to our table after our food arrived), and our waters were never refilled. The place was fairly busy but it was a Wednesday evening at 6pm. Overall I would say this place is ok if you get pasta, but they really need to improve their service.</Text>

<user>114066658291767162801< /user><user_name>bruce chia< /user_name><date>1507996454906< /date><Rate>4< /Rate>< Text>
The restaurant is a really big space inside a hotel so it may not be as easy to get to. We went on a lazy Sunday afternoon so there were very few guests. The service staff was small for the big space so they had to walk around a lot, making the service slow but I don't blame them, especially since they have a nice row of window seats facing the VTA train outside. The bread they served before the meal was cold, and not nice to eat, but an old waiter came around to give us olive oil and vinegar which was nice. I ordered a chicken pasta and it was actually quite delicious. I ordered it as Secondi (a smaller portion) and it came out perfectly sized, just enough for me. You may want a Primi portion if you are hungry.<//Text>

< Review>
We had dinner at Il Fornaio on Friday evening and it was a disappointing dining experience.
The restaurant wasn't very busy when we arrived, but it took the front door a while to seat us.   It then took our server a while to take our drink order, and by then we were ready to order our entrees.
Bread came warm to the table, which was one of the highlights of the meal.  My cannellini bean soup was the other highlight - rich, hearty, and flavorful.
3 out of the 4 entrees were less than expected - the meat in my bolognese sauce was very dry.  My friend got the grilled salmon (on the specials menu) and it was overcooked.  The spinach that came with it looked like it was previously frozen - it was gray and wilted.  My husband got the rigatoni with the vodka cream sauce and it was just meh.  The dishes lacked presentation and flavor, and several items were overcooked.
Service was cordial but on the slower side.
I don't think we'll return to Il Fornaio any time soon.</Review>
